        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341271376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6230798161632567497">Thirst No.3: The Eternal Dawn:<br/>As always, I give this book a five-star rating. The Thirst series just gets better and better.<br/>In the beginning of this story, Sita is back and better than ever, ready to murder a rapist whose next victim is her SUPER-great granddaughter, Teri Raine, a descendant of her only human child, Lalita. After disposing of good ole’ Danny Boy—Daniel Buford, an aspiring football and track star with a secret life as a rapist—by drowning him in a lake where he had previously san</span>
  <span id="freeText6230798161632567497" style="display:none">Thirst No.3: The Eternal Dawn:<br />As always, I give this book a five-star rating. The Thirst series just gets better and better.<br />In the beginning of this story, Sita is back and better than ever, ready to murder a rapist whose next victim is her SUPER-great granddaughter, Teri Raine, a descendant of her only human child, Lalita. After disposing of good ole’ Danny Boy—Daniel Buford, an aspiring football and track star with a secret life as a rapist—by drowning him in a lake where he had previously sank all his other victims, Sita introduces herself to Teri, knowing her involvement in Teri’s life may cause her danger, but she cannot resist, feeling lonely. Offering Teri a false job as her researcher, she says her name is Alisa Perne and that she is a writer working on her first novel and needs someone to do her medical references for her because she simply does not have time to look up all the facts. Teri is excited by the offer but first wants the opinion of her boyfriend, Matt, and invites Alisa to her him sing at one of his gigs. Meanwhile, when Sita returns home that afternoon, she notices a pot knocked over at her house, a sign someone has been around, yet nothing but that clue indicates a person coming by. Suspicious, Sita goes to get a gun when Lisa Fetch and her boyfriend Jeff Stephens come to inform her about a company named IIC (Infinite Investment Corporation) and their interest in her. Sita is wary but not all too worried and hires people to do research on the case for her. She goes to the Gator, a club, to hear Matt sing and listens to Teri talking to him backstage. Immediately, Sita catches on Matt’s strong sense of intuition and later admires his songwriting, as he is extremely talented and very charismatic. After his show, Teri, Matt, and Sita sit down to talk and get to know each other better as they all discuss one of Sita’s short stories, written under the pen name Lara Adams—the same name she used when she introduced herself to Ray.<br />When Sita returns home that night, she is assaulted by an unknown assassin who nearly murders her with his impressive skill and destructive Gatling gun. Thankfully, Sita’s quick thinking and remarkable wit allow her to devise a plan to escape her house and kill her assailant even after being shot in the liver. Later the man is revealed to be Claudious Ember and kills himself using a suicide tooth in his mouth. Four days later, Matt and Teri meet Sita at her new house—her old one exploded in a diversion she attempted to create—and Matt sings Sita another one of his songs while she lets him read another one of her stories. Sita finds herself undeniably attracted to Matt, wanting him, but restrains herself for Teri’s sake. <br />A former FBI agent working for Sita finds a lead from Switzerland connected to Claudious Ember, leading to a man named Marko, a hired assassin. Sita lures him out of his house shortly after arriving there and interrogates him, finding a lead on his boss and a girl named Shanti. She visits the girl the next day under the name of Special Agent Jessica Reese and tells Shanti and her uncle that a man named Marko was hired to kill Shanti. The reason is unknown, but Shanti’s uncle, Shivam Garuda, agrees on hiring protection for Shanti, whose face is terribly disfigured by an incident involving sulfuric acid from a car battery thrown at her by her former fiancé, Juna, whom she tried to escape marrying and thus was attacked by him in her birth country, India. That afternoon, Sita gets a call from her friend Lisa and is informed that Jeff has not contacted her even though he promised he would, leaving Lisa very concerned. Sita forces Lisa to stay put, knowing they are in danger, by using her psychic powers, and heads to IIC, located in Malibu, California. There she is left waiting to meet the boss, Mrs. Cynthia Brutran, and a strange lady asks Sita to hold her child, Athena, while she uses the restroom. However, Athena becomes restless and smashes a vase while her mother is not present, and Sita tries to pick the glass shards out of the child, yet the mother returns and grows terribly angry with Sita, leaving in a hurry. After a brief but hostile confrontation with Brutran, Sita storms out and goes to meet Lisa. She investigates his house and confirms that he has been murdered using her super senses, which devastates Lisa. Convinced that she is next, Sita forbids Lisa to attend work and changes her name. <br />Later, Sita camps outside IIC, waiting for Brutran to leave work, but she seems to never do so, using the building as her fortress. Sita recalls some earlier events involving Teri and Matt and calls Lisa. Finally Brutran leaves work and returns to her house, which is surprisingly unarmed. At all. Sita knows it is suspicious. She runs into Brutran’s little girl in the hallway, who is creepy… and is attacked by the Array, a secret IIC weapon, while talking to Brutran, who reveals plans to save mankind. Sita somehow does not die, possibly by thinking of Krishna her dying moments. <br />Somewhere along the way, Shanti, Lisa, Matt, Teri, and Sita become a little gang, and when Sita gives Teri her vampire blood to give her extra strength to win the Olympics, one of her dreams, Teri seems to do well. However, there are also side effects… Meanwhile, Shanti undergoes facial repairs, courtesy of Sita, and Sita reconciles with Seymour, revealing the truth of how this book could possibly exist after Sita magically became human at the end of the last novel and died a mortal. Apparently the first two books were stories Seymour wrote about Sita through their telepathic connection, but they never really met in reality. Seymour, though he has an advanced case of AIDS, still lives, and after he believes it is really Sita, he joins their little gang. Sita gives Teri more of her blood to win the Olympics.<br />Shortly after Teri’s victory, four assassins from the same source as Claudious Ember come after Sita and she forces her way into the hotel where the president is staying to buy protection with the Secret Service. But the assassins manipulate the agents using their psychic powers similar to Sita’s, and Sita must take them out herself. She kills both male assassins and one female, then gets permission from Mike, head of the Service security, to chase down the remaining assassin. The woman takes a ferry, but Sita swims quickly enough to intercept her, attack, and take the woman as a hostage to interrogate. Using Sodium Pentothal, Sita treats the woman’s wounds—who reveals herself as Numbria—and gets her to spill everything she knows about the people she works for. They are the Telar, and they wish to destroy mankind, old as the beginning of time itself. Sita drifts into half-sleep and is seized by the Array, which plunges her into a nightmare about Lucifer and she wakes delirious with madness and hunger, making her ruthlessly murder Numbria and attempt to do the same to Seymour and Shanti, who come to help her. After Shanti calms Sita down, Matt and Teri walk in on them… and they see Numbria’s mangled body on the bed, caked with blood and torn flesh, and Sita’s face, covered with dried blood. There is only one horrific assumption to make, and Teri nearly passes out. Matt is calm yet angry, as if he knew what Sita was all along. And perhaps he does…<br />Seymour and Sita go to visit Paula and John shortly later. John has grown up and is now sixteen. He is playing a video game called CII (Cosmic Intuitive Illusion) and will not see Sita, but sees Seymour. Sita and Paula talk, and as usual, Paula is infuriatingly vague. Seymour makes a comment that suggests CII may be of importance to the story in an underlying way. <br />Sita travels to Arosa, Switzerland with Shanti after her visit to Santorini, Greece, where she follows a lead on Yaksha. Apparently, as she found out from Numbria, Yaksha was married to a Telar. Surprise! Anyway, a man who owns a hotel named Horace (Herr) Reinhart recognizes the portrait of Yaksha Sita paints and allows her access into his old workspace, where she cracks the code to his vault. Inside is a large book of his life, and the code to the vault is shocking: <i>I love you, Sita.</i> Yaksha’s book contains many important truths about life, and the Telar want it, as Sita discovers. She makes a copy of the book and sends Shanti off to Seymour with it before returning the original to Herr Reinhart and disobeying his request for her to leave the vault open. When she locks it back into the safe, he locks her into the room, revealing his true identity as a Telar. <br />After two days, Sita is visited by the head Telar, or the leader of the Source, whose name is Haru. He reveals himself as Umara’s brother, Umara being the wife of Yaksha. Yaksha and Umara defied authority by being together, and as a punishment, the Telar burned Umara and her son, Keshava. Sita, understandably, is jealous of Umara—she confesses she wishes she was the one who had Yaksha’s child. Haru puts Sita through intense questioning, and even though Sita answers the majority of Haru’s questions, he uses a terrible machine as destructive as the IIC’s Array on Sita. It is called the Pulse, and it taps into the brain’s pain center to cause the victim to forget their sense of identity. Sita undergoes intense pain, vomits, and pisses on herself while being shocked with level three and five settings of the Pulse. The highest setting is ten, and it causes permanent brain damage. However, when Haru turns the dial up to eight, Sita is able to withstand the pain by thinking of staring into Krishna’s blue eyes, considered to be the highest form of Hindu meditation. Haru is shocked, refusing to believe that love and kindness are the sources of being able to block out both the Pulse and the Array.<br />Matt rescues Sita, revealing himself as Keshava, Yaksha’s supposedly dead son, revealing many revelations and causing many things to make sense. They return to Teri, Seymour, and Shanti, who all know the truth of what they’re up against, and prepare to fight the Telar. They take out the first onslaught of Haru’s Telar soldiers, but then three Telar release a supervirus designed to destroy the majority of humanity; the Telar want to destroy humanity and are therefore the enemies of the IIC, who want to save humanity. Yet both groups are highly evil and have super weapons. Sita finds the vaccine for the supervirus by kidnapping a Telar scientist named Charlie, who begins to help them, and injects Teri, Matt, Seymour, Shanti, and herself. Then they all take to the air in Matt’s escape helicopter and flee. But they are tailed by more Telar and Sita has a plan to jump out of the helicopter and into the lake below, like she had with Joel on the run. Sita, Shanti, Seymour, and Charlie jump successfully, but Teri fractures her leg and begins dying in a cave. Charlie and Shanti go to get Matt, who drove the helicopter elsewhere, and Sita turns Teri into a vampire. When Matt arrives, the Array seizes him and turns him against Sita, whom he kills in his misguided anger. The book ends with Seymour and everyone else—Lisa, Matt, Teri, Shanti, Paula, John—at Sita’s funeral, and once everyone leaves, Seymour remains. Teri doubles back to find him and whispers a secret in his ear: she is Sita in Teri’s body. So of course, I cannot wait for Thirst No. 4! It just gets better and better! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6230798161632567497" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2677274139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2677274139" />
    <a title="TheVeryBookish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22781517-theverybookish"><img alt="TheVeryBookish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546587288p2/22781517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2677274139?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheVeryBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheVeryBookish" href="/user/show/22781517-theverybookish">TheVeryBookish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2677274139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5100321242063379845">The plot of this novel was okay for the most part but a little bit of a contradictory aspect bothered me regarding this. As in the main character wanting to meet and get close to a certain person but not wanting to cause trouble but KNOWING she would... yeah, that kind of thing. *eye roll*(8/10)<br/><br/>The writing style and flow were good but a few times there were moments when Sita wanted to refer to Teri as her daughter and I really disliked this a lot and it interrupted how I was feeling about the re</span>
  <span id="freeText5100321242063379845" style="display:none">The plot of this novel was okay for the most part but a little bit of a contradictory aspect bothered me regarding this. As in the main character wanting to meet and get close to a certain person but not wanting to cause trouble but KNOWING she would... yeah, that kind of thing. *eye roll*(8/10)<br /><br />The writing style and flow were good but a few times there were moments when Sita wanted to refer to Teri as her daughter and I really disliked this a lot and it interrupted how I was feeling about the rest of what was going on at the time. I found that specific thing weird and not very understandable. (8.5/10)<br /><br />The atmosphere/world building was consistent with the previous installments, no difficulties immersing in the world of Sita and the others. (8.5/10)<br /><br />New characters introduced in this book were okay but I personally felt like Teri was just pretty dull and not very interesting at all or defined. She was just eh. Matt was at least interesting and mysterious and saved the rating from being a bit lower. (8/10)<br /><br />The logical overview of this story was the worst part in my opinion. Kind of reflects back on what I said about the plot, Sita knew she would cause trouble by involving herself with Teri and Matt and yet even though she complained about not wanting to do just that and knowing she would... she continued to do it anyway and put them in danger. Some of Sita's behavior also seemed out of the ordinary and maybe it's the fact Teri is her relative and that makes her a little less strict with herself. I'm not sure but it bothered me a bit that I felt like some of the actions weren't what I feel like would be the decision she made. (6/10)<br /><br />Overall, I still really enjoyed the ride of the story. I think some things could have been better and I didn't think it was as good as the first two novels. There are multiple books in the series, but it's worth noting that the first two books can almost be a finished story in itself unless you're just curious for more Sita, then you can continue with this one. (9/10)<br /><br /><b> 8.1/10 rating </b><br /><i> Thanks to BookRoast for the CAWPILE rating system! </i></span>

<div id="review_3219594550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3219594550" />
    <a title="Allie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93274243-allie"><img alt="Allie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3219594550?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allie" href="/user/show/93274243-allie">Allie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3219594550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6886689210533216948">This book BLEW my mind!!! But the ending... I don’t know. I have my doubts. <br/>The book is just WILD; so much action, so many plot twists and quirky characters that I absolutely adore. I LOVE that Alisa isn’t alone anymore and is surrounded by her friends (she was so motherly and nurturing, I loved this side of her!). But at the same time, it feels like the storyline is just strung along. It feels repetitive too; Sita is invincible, then out of nowhere there’s a stronger enemy but eventually she be</span>
  <span id="freeText6886689210533216948" style="display:none">This book BLEW my mind!!! But the ending... I don’t know. I have my doubts. <br />The book is just WILD; so much action, so many plot twists and quirky characters that I absolutely adore. I LOVE that Alisa isn’t alone anymore and is surrounded by her friends (she was so motherly and nurturing, I loved this side of her!). But at the same time, it feels like the storyline is just strung along. It feels repetitive too; Sita is invincible, then out of nowhere there’s a stronger enemy but eventually she beats them, then she’s invincible again. But wait; here comes another enemy... and again, and again. <br />Also, sometimes I didn’t really know what was happening because it got so complicated, it wasn’t always easy to follow; so many new character names and organization names (IIC, the Telar, the Source, the Array, ...). It felt like Pike got overexcited, which is great because it shows he’s passionate about his work, but the audience just ended up being bulldozed with a bunch of information, which wasn’t pleasant. <br />So what I’m trying to say is; there’s so many exciting things happening, such a wide variety, but at the same time I find it boring because it’s always the same patterns and it becomes quite predictable. <br />I’m very unmotivated to read book number 4. I need to take a break from this series for a while, maybe I’ll read the rest later. I don’t feel like reading about the IIC and the Telar again; it should’ve stopped in book 3, there’s not enough happening to keep me interested.<br />If the book wouldn’t have those constant repetitive parts, I would give it 5 stars for SURE! But it does, so a 3 seemed appropriate. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6886689210533216948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Alicia Croft" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25257464-alicia-croft"><img alt="Alicia Croft" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539663364p2/25257464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2458702095?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia Croft" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia Croft" href="/user/show/25257464-alicia-croft">Alicia Croft</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2458702095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3842208318009804798">Im a huge fan of The Last Vampire series. While I enjoyed this book, and I expected to - I'm a fan of this author from my teen years, but I had a few problems with this book. <br/><br/>First and foremost, the premise of continuing Sita's story after the original series meant betraying the readers trust, and destroying the integrity of the original series. I wanted to accept the premise, because I wanted more of Sitas story, but it left a bad taste. I felt a loss over the change in Seymour and Sita's histo</span>
  <span id="freeText3842208318009804798" style="display:none">Im a huge fan of The Last Vampire series. While I enjoyed this book, and I expected to - I'm a fan of this author from my teen years, but I had a few problems with this book. <br /><br />First and foremost, the premise of continuing Sita's story after the original series meant betraying the readers trust, and destroying the integrity of the original series. I wanted to accept the premise, because I wanted more of Sitas story, but it left a bad taste. I felt a loss over the change in Seymour and Sita's history, and I dont think reading the first series will ever be the same again.<br /><br />It also required a lot more buy-in from the reader - it got much more sci-fi, a lot more bizzare than a typical YA vampire novel - Pike's books are always alternative anyway - a kind of new-age/spiritual vampire series, but im not sure I liked the additional christian-hellish darkness and alien talk. The olympics was a stretch - I dont know how that will play out in further books with Sita being in Terri's body - or even how Terri managed to avoid press etc in the aftermath of a gold medal. <br /><br />I still enjoyed it - I dont want to criticise, because I love Sita (even if she's way less bad ass these days). I really enjoy the way Pikes mind works, I do love his unbelievable plots - but this was just a touch more unbelievability than I expected I guess. I really love the first few - I would have probably preferred a prequel than mashing up the first books, and claiming they didnt really happen like that.. sigh.. How can I dislike so many elements, but still enjoy the book?? </span>
  <a data-text-id="3842208318009804798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('e62BNvZwDOuYStRlrGxXl79qTApplIwq3Vrlr8z9suBKnkY5fwJDV3tiH6A+kMuHhpq49UInSHnIhQwEZ6FQXw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cgvweG52KaB7fG8Pj1bVG0UyvZTQlFYH5jaEuoOSrDhDODd35wRmHJhUpModqkkLfMJJa/snklTz6W0RKM5Ohw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2980410762679779266">Christopher Pike is the pseudonym of Kevin McFadden. He is a bestselling author of young adult and children's fiction who specializes in the thriller genre.<br/><br/><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i> <br/><br/>McFadden was born in New York but grew up in California where he stills lives in today. A college drop-out, he did factory work, painted houses and programm</span>
  <span id="freeText2980410762679779266" style="display:none">Christopher Pike is the pseudonym of Kevin McFadden. He is a bestselling author of young adult and children's fiction who specializes in the thriller genre.<br /><br /><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name.</i> <br /><br />McFadden was born in New York but grew up in California where he stills lives in today. A college drop-out, he did factory work, painted houses and programmed computers before becoming a recognized author. Initially unsuccessful when he set out to write science fiction and adult mystery, it was not until his work caught the attention of an editor who suggested he write a teen thriller that he became a hit. The result was Slumber Party (1985), a book about a group of teenagers who run into bizarre and violent events during a ski weekend. After that he wrote Weekend and Chain Letter. All three books went on to become bestsellers.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/10682093-the-eternal-dawn">Quotes from Thirst No. 3: The...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;No one awakens in the morning thinking they will die that day. Not a saint or a sinner. Not even a condemned killer. We all know were mortal, and yet we all believe we'll live forever.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/346609-no-one-awakens-in-the-morning-thinking-they-will-die">74 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I think of Krishna and his deep blue eyes. It is said, in the hidden scriptures in India, that to focus on the eyes of the Lord is the highest spiritual practice a human being can proform. It's suppose to be equal to the greatest act of charity, which Jesus describes in the Bible as sacrificing one's life to save the life of another.<br /><br />The Vedas, the Bible, it's true, they overlap a lot.<br /><br />Maybe gazing into Krishna's eyes...<br /><br />Pain...Pain...Pain...<br /><br />Is equal to Christ's sacrifice.<br /><br />I'm only suffering this pain to protect John. It doesn't matter that he won't see me. I still love him, I will always love him. And in this exquisitely agonizing moment, I realize he refused to see me because he wanted to force me to see him inside. Ah, that's the key! This practice of visualizing that I'm staring into Krishna's blue eyes, I've done it before.<br /><br />But this is the first time I see him staring back at me!<br /><br />The Agony comes, and it does not get transformed into bliss.<br /><br />If anything it is worse than before. Except for one thing.<br /><br />The pain does not obliterate my sense of "I."<br /><br />I'm still Sita, the last vampire.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/645977-i-think-of-krishna-and-his-deep-blue-eyes-it">22 likes</a>
            </nobr>
